        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer810132387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4289155300705234363">Strangely, perhaps my favourite of the Witcher novels (then of course not counting the ultimate masterpiece that is <i>The Last Wish</i>). There is something that draws me in about <i>The Time of Contempt</i>. Something I remember more fondly than the rest. It is slightly enigmatic, filled with intrigue and an overall sense of mystery.<br/><br/>As the most sorcery-centric and Yennefer-centric book of them all, it is no wonder that I would enjoy it quite a lot, but it also contains some rather memorable and world-shakin</span>
  <span id="freeText4289155300705234363" style="display:none">Strangely, perhaps my favourite of the Witcher novels (then of course not counting the ultimate masterpiece that is <i>The Last Wish</i>). There is something that draws me in about <i>The Time of Contempt</i>. Something I remember more fondly than the rest. It is slightly enigmatic, filled with intrigue and an overall sense of mystery.<br /><br />As the most sorcery-centric and Yennefer-centric book of them all, it is no wonder that I would enjoy it quite a lot, but it also contains some rather memorable and world-shaking moments integral to the development of this exquisite setting. The 'incident' on Thanedd Isle alone is astonishingly well written, and takes up a significant portion of the book.<br /><br />I suspect I shall have to read this again, at which point I may elaborate on the beauty of this gem. It certainly is, however, one of the most considerable successes by an author attempting to write a middle book without a whiff of second book syndrome.<br /><br /><b>Witcher reviews:</b><br />#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792532185" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a><br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890591117" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a><br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793290591" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a><br />#4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/810132387" rel="nofollow noopener">Time of Contempt</a><br />#5 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/866619209" rel="nofollow noopener">Baptism of Fire</a><br />#6 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200252982" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tower of the Swallow</a><br />#7 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200252988" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady of the Lake</a><br />#0 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2404193589" rel="nofollow noopener">Season of Storms</a></span>

<div id="review_1353190706" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353190706" />
    <a title="Alex " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1808983-alex"><img alt="Alex " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455804079p2/1808983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219136" href="/book/show/14781491-the-time-of-contempt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1808983-alex?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353190706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15742306232172004930">Apparently these books are rather big in Poland. I know this because a Polish woman told me so. Apparently there are some rather successful videogames that have been based on these books. I know this because I've played one of them. It was good.<br/><br/>Clearly these books have never been that big in the West, they haven't even all been translated yet and they were written in the early 90s, and it makes you doubt what's going on in the fantasy book publishing world. It makes you wonder if there's a profo</span>
  <span id="freeText15742306232172004930" style="display:none">Apparently these books are rather big in Poland. I know this because a Polish woman told me so. Apparently there are some rather successful videogames that have been based on these books. I know this because I've played one of them. It was good.<br /><br />Clearly these books have never been that big in the West, they haven't even all been translated yet and they were written in the early 90s, and it makes you doubt what's going on in the fantasy book publishing world. It makes you wonder if there's a profoundly US/UK-centric bias and that publishers don't love fantasy literature per-se they just love kissing the arse of George R.R.Martin and Steven King. No wait, they just love making money and you can't make money from a Polish book, can you?<br /><br />It's a shame, the lack of hype surrounding these books, because they are really rather good; both well written, highly original and dare I say it ahead of their time. On the face of it these books are steeped in the usual cliche, magicians, elves, swordsmen, monsters and a chosen child litter the pages and you'll find a lot of what you expected to find when perusing an extended fantasy epic series. No, these books don't reinvent the wheel but rather than running around and around it, doing the same old song and dance, they certainly have a bit of fun with it.<br /><br />Firstly, these books are a weird mish-mash hybrid of fantasy styles. The Witcher, Geralt, is your typical brooding, loner, Sword and Sorcery protagonist making his way in a dangerous world filled with monsters. You'd expect him to be out there earning money and bedding women. And he is, until he gets a fixation with the young child Ciri and decides to raise her as a Witcher. Genres clash and much of the tale is told from Ciri, the chosen one's point of view and we spend time watching her grow up in a dangerous and alien world. On top of this there are poltical machinations aplenty, perhaps not as indepth or steeped in history as ASOIAF but they colour a traditional S&amp;S text in interesting ways and send the story veering off in directions at time one doesn't expect.<br /><br />Secondly these books are stylistically very odd. It's a 5 book series but really they make up one whole rambling story and not individual chapters, each volume so far has just ended in the middle with no indicators or allusions to the end of this, or the beginning of the next volume. More relevantly, the books have a weird episodic feel to them and each chapter tends to tell a scene that is only loosely connected to those around it, but taken as a whole the larger narrative slots into place very elegantly. Each chapter tends to be told in a dramatically different style and the story can easily shift from action scene, to political intrigue, to coming of age tale to sketchy flashback narratives. It's audacious and I wonder sometimes if it really all works, but what's exciting is that the story constantly feels fresh and whilst one usually knows where these kinds of narratives are heading, there's an air of ambiguity and interest here that 80s fantasy epics began to lack.<br /><br />This is a series that really bridges the high fantasy of the 80s with the gritty politics of the late 90s and as such it deserves to be read more. I've only so far read the first two volumes (didn't review 1 because it didn't feel self-contained( but at this point I expect the quality to be maintained and this to be a thrilling ride to the finish. Worth seeking out even though it hasn't actually been translated yet. Sorry, what's that all about again?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15742306232172004930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1995421643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995421643" />
    <a title="Celise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653644-celise"><img alt="Celise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546382482p2/4653644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1995421643?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celise" href="/user/show/4653644-celise">Celise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219136" href="/book/show/14781491-the-time-of-contempt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=fantasy-adult">fantasy-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1995421643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer496313250340570156">I feel like doing a super informal review for this one, just because this writer makes me feel so many feelings and The Witcher is on the fast-track to becoming my favourite series so quickly that I don't know how to put my thoughts into presentable order. So here's a bunch of words for you, and a few run-on sentences most likely. It's not gushy, I promise, just ineloquent. My review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917549623?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Blood of Elves</a> is probably a better recommendation of the series.<br/><br/>Ciri, Geralt, and Yennefer are some of my</span>
  <span id="freeText496313250340570156" style="display:none">I feel like doing a super informal review for this one, just because this writer makes me feel so many feelings and The Witcher is on the fast-track to becoming my favourite series so quickly that I don't know how to put my thoughts into presentable order. So here's a bunch of words for you, and a few run-on sentences most likely. It's not gushy, I promise, just ineloquent. My review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917549623?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blood of Elves</a> is probably a better recommendation of the series.<br /><br />Ciri, Geralt, and Yennefer are some of my favourite literary characters. I don't ship anyone in anything more than I ship Geralt and Yennefer. I even enjoy Triss and Geralt a little. I think I love Ciri as much as I love Daenerys. After reading The Last Wish I took issue with the way that Sapkowski presented women. Not represented, because they were always developed, but I definitely thought some objectification was going on. That has been remedied for me with The Blood of Elves and The Time of Contempt, and I think I'll go back to that previous review and make note of that. I honestly didn't expect my mind to change on that one. Sapkowski is actually really good at writing developed female characters, and there are many of them.<br /><br />The politics in this series are also easy to understand but unpredictable, which is ideal. They're not as complex as something George R.R. Martin would write, but they're not as basic as "these two countries are at war, here's a story about some characters who are involved". The minimal magic is also totally up my alley. I love fantasy, but I've never been a huge fan of magic in the genre. The Witcher mutation is super cool though, and when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ciri used her magic in the desert)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I lost my shit. That was great. Overall though I love that these are more supernatural than magical.<br /><br /> My favourite part was probably the desert. I've never enjoyed a desert scene more than I enjoyed that one (and I just had a terrible reading experience with another book set in a desert and was not primed or excited when Sapkowski started describing that setting). There were just some great character building moments in that chapter, and it reminded me a little bit of some of the short stories in the anthologies, with there being monsters and all. And Little Horse! I wish there were more monsters/supernatural creatures like there were in the short stories but that's my only complaint. The novels are bigger picture than those, so I get it.<br /><br />Switching tones now, and I don't have a proper segue.<br /><br />I think it was implied in Blood of Elves that Ciri was attracted to Geralt, in that childish innocence kind of way. She was very jealous of Yennefer, and both Yenn and Triss kind of hinted at Ciri's infatuation. At least that's my take. I doubt it's going anywhere, but I thought it was fun to read because it makes sense. This man rescues her from helplessness and trains her to be a badass; naturally she's going to be jealous of this beautiful woman that Geralt also gives attention to. I'm sure as she gets older the infatuation will fade and it'll resemble more of a father/daughter relationship. It's totally normal for girls to have crushes on older people they idolize. My shipper brain sort of wishes they were a thing, but like not actually? <br /><br />Ciri's romantic/sexual developments are always curious to me, especially because I think this male author did such a fantastic job. I was a little upset about the ending of this one, but I understand how it happened. I wasn't going to comment on it but ahh, Sapkowski just makes me care too much. So here's for the icky bit. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />The ending of this book disturbed me. If Ciri is bisexual I'd be totally up for it. More LGBT characters in fantasy please! But that scene was REALLY RAPEY. Mistle (female) saves Ciri from being raped by Kaleigh (male) but then rapes her herself. This little girl is scared and alone, about to be raped by this dude. Along comes this woman who sends him packing, putting herself in the position of saviour, then lays down with Ciri herself. She's already traumatized and Mistle seems the better option over Kaleigh. Ciri who is young, scared, and curious is kind of into it for a second, which happens to people and makes sense, but Mistle totally took advantage of her. Not cool. Ciri washing herself off in the morning and feeling all bad made me so fucking mad/sad/upset (for Ciri, not at the author. I think he wrote it well, more subtly and less glorifying than many authors).<br /><br />I'm not sure what I expected. All of the relationships are so angsty that Ciri was going to have something bad happen to her at some point. I'm happy that the author doesn't shy away from that shit. If the next book picks up in the same place, or if the incident is ever mentioned again, I hope that he treats things properly. He's been really good with his female characters so far, but I'm still nervous. I don't know, maybe it'll become some Daenerys/Drogo complex (which admittedly I shipped so hard), and if it's handled well by the author then that's fine. I just feel so bad for Ciri. Who knows, maybe it's never mentioned again. It just seems like he was setting up The Rats to be characters in the next one, which I'm up for. Maybe I'm a horrible person but I enjoy being made to feel like crap over my favourite characters. Just handle it well, please.<br /><br />I know that characters don't need love interests to be interesting, especially in this genre, but Yennefer and Geralt are just such a fascinating love story that I expect it out of Sapkowski to do something like that for Ciri, who now seems to be his main character. I just want her to fall in love with some awesome character, male or female. Give me that please!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Uh so, for the sake of pretending that this was at all a review: I recommend this series! George R.R. Martin fans, get it. Patrick Rothfuss fans, get it (maybe? This series has that character growing up and learning their craft element, just seems like a similar subgenre). Except this is better (in my opinion, obviously). Video game nerds (you were probably already here before me), get it! For a better review, check out the one I wrote for Blood of Elves linked below. I don't know what happened here.<br /><br />Reading order/Previous reviews:<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851073182?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890613485?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Destiny</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917549623?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Blood of Elves</a><br />The Time of Contempt<br />Baptism of Fire<br />The Tower of Swallows/The Tower of the Swallow/The Swallow's Tower <br />The Lady of the Lake</span>
  <a data-text-id="496313250340570156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3214013942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3214013942" />
    <a title="Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70046142-elle"><img alt="Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548160841p2/70046142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3214013942?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle" href="/user/show/70046142-elle">Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219136" href="/book/show/14781491-the-time-of-contempt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3214013942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3563266268149934906">This one felt like a lot of preamble. I gave some of the slower parts in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043781.Blood_of_Elves__The_Witcher___1_' title='Blood of Elves (The Witcher, #1) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blood of Elves</a> a pass because it had the more difficult task of transitioning from short stories to novels & being the first in the novel series, but what’s the excuse here?? The entire first half of the book felt like nothing was happening and wow it just draaaaaagged. <br/><br/>And maybe I was just zoned out for the relevant stuff, but by the time the big second-act battle started up, I had no idea what was happening. I didn’t know</span>
  <span id="freeText3563266268149934906" style="display:none">This one felt like a lot of preamble. I gave some of the slower parts in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6043781.Blood_of_Elves__The_Witcher___1_" title="Blood of Elves (The Witcher, #1) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a> a pass because it had the more difficult task of transitioning from short stories to novels &amp; being the first in the novel series, but what’s the excuse here?? The entire first half of the book felt like nothing was happening and wow it just draaaaaagged. <br /><br />And maybe I was just zoned out for the relevant stuff, but by the time the big second-act battle started up, I had no idea what was happening. I didn’t know who anyone was or why they were fighting or who was winning and which side I was supposed to be cheering for. Geralt, as usual, decided to sit on his hands when it came time to make ~*~dEsCiSiOnS~*, so I ended up just going along with whatever name I recognized. <i>Oh, Triss! I know her! Get em, Triss! Wait, that’s Tissaia, I know her too! Are Triss and Tissaia fighting? Now I’m confused.</i> Idk<br /><br />And I am unable to not keep pointing this out—Sapkowski doesn’t grasp how women interact with one another. The way the enchantresses spoke and moved around that party in the third chapter was just cringy. “<i>‘Oh you men . . . You don’t understand anything. How can you show off your dress or figure if you’re hiding behind a table in the glow and smoke?’</i>“ Like, what woman would say this type of thing? Out loud?? To other humans??? They’re supposed to be all-powerful and brilliant! Unless, of course, they come across some jewelry or eyeshadow, then they devolve into squealing, vapid tarts, amiright?<br /><br /> I also absolutely hated the way he wrote Yennefer as a jealous, petty bitch and Triss as a skittish animal in need of a good kicking. Geralt comes off as absolutely pathetic here, like a lost, horny boy that’s never seen boobs before. How can you tell a fantasy series is written through the male gaze? No woman would end a description of a dress like this: “<i>Fashion demanded it be split halfway up the thigh, but Sabrina wore hers split to halfway up her hip. <b>And a very nice hip at that.</b></i>” These errant thoughts are eyeroll-inducing, but hard to miss once you begin to notice them. <br /><br />There was good stuff too, lest you think I’m just gonna rag on it the whole time. Dandelion playing interpreter for Ciri during Geralt and Yennefer’s fight was a bit of unexpected sweetness I didn’t know I needed. Dandelion, that little weed, has definitely grown on me. Yennefer when she’s not being possessive is wonderful, and I love Ciri’s feralness. Geralt was kind of lame in this one. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[My favorite chapter is weirdly the one where Ciri is wandering around a desert with a Unicorn, eating bugs and being friends like Timon &amp; Pumba. It was tedious, but I also couldn’t get enough???? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />At this point, I can’t really help imagining each scene as it would play out in the TV series. I just think Lauren Schmidt Hissrich is going to really nail some of parts where Sapkowski floundered, like the aforementioned party. I’m also going to need Netflix to announce some upcoming casting decisions ASAP so I can start pairing names with faces—hopefully that’ll help me keep some of these Polish names straight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3563266268149934906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320490606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6780929733808471477">This is the second full-length instalment to The Witcher series.<br/><br/>Where has the story-line I was promised in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_' title='The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Wish</a> gone? What happened to my beast-slaying Witcher?<br/><br/>Whilst not an unenjoyable read, this was also not the tale I thought I was signing up for. The first prequel short story collection seemed to set this series up as being one thing when in fact it was the the second collection, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25454056.Sword_of_Destiny__The_Witcher___0_75_' title='Sword of Destiny (The Witcher, #0.75) by Andrzej Sapkowski' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sword of Destiny</a>, which was far slower in pace and more romantically focused, that better gave an indica</span>
  <span id="freeText6780929733808471477" style="display:none">This is the second full-length instalment to The Witcher series.<br /><br />Where has the story-line I was promised in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40603587.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___0_5_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #0.5) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a> gone? What happened to my beast-slaying Witcher?<br /><br />Whilst not an unenjoyable read, this was also not the tale I thought I was signing up for. The first prequel short story collection seemed to set this series up as being one thing when in fact it was the the second collection, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25454056.Sword_of_Destiny__The_Witcher___0_75_" title="Sword of Destiny (The Witcher, #0.75) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">Sword of Destiny</a>, which was far slower in pace and more romantically focused, that better gave an indication for the later focus. <br /><br />The events here were largely focused not around the Witcher, Geralt, as anticipated, but around the child of prophecy, Ciri. Despite being one of my favourite characters in this series I was always eager to return to Geralt's perspective but little of the plot progression actually stemmed there.<br /><br />The full first half was very slow in pace but the latter did increase in scenes of action and tension. It left off on a cliffhanger that has me inclined to believe this more political focus, which has a historical fiction feel to it in places, will also permeate through the rest of the series and, unfortunately, it is not something I care to continue with. Definitely not a bad read, just different to the one I came here for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6780929733808471477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3051099127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3051099127" />
    <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe"><img alt="Amanda Hupe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535036536p2/11658047.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3051099127?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Hupe" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe">Amanda Hupe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316219136" href="/book/show/14781491-the-time-of-contempt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3051099127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6798363149027921767">The Time of Contempt by Andrzej Sapkowski is the second book in The Witcher Series. Rumor has it that the show will only consist of The Last Wish, Sword of Destiny, and Blood of Elves. So now I am ahead of the game!<br/><br/>For those just tuning in…Geralt is a witcher. He is made to take down the most ferocious of monsters. Now his destiny lies with Ciri, a young girl whose future will determine the fate of the world. He must protect her at all costs. However, war has been declared everywhere. There are </span>
  <span id="freeText6798363149027921767" style="display:none">The Time of Contempt by Andrzej Sapkowski is the second book in The Witcher Series. Rumor has it that the show will only consist of The Last Wish, Sword of Destiny, and Blood of Elves. So now I am ahead of the game!<br /><br />For those just tuning in…Geralt is a witcher. He is made to take down the most ferocious of monsters. Now his destiny lies with Ciri, a young girl whose future will determine the fate of the world. He must protect her at all costs. However, war has been declared everywhere. There are those who seek Ciri for their own gains and Geralt can’t trust anyone. Ciri is a young woman now and determined to forge her own path. Yennefer, an enchantress assists Geralt with keeping Ciri out of sight. However, the Wizard’s Guild deals with a coup. Geralt and Ciri are separated and both in danger.<br /><br />I really need maps. Maps and graphs. The world-building is so incredible that I feel like I need some sort of guide while I am reading. Sorcerers are under the control of kings, who are always declaring war on one another. So I think before I start the next book, I am going to do a little studying so I can have a better idea of all the politics.<br /><br />Onto the characters. I still don’t like Yennefer. Am I missing something about her? She doesn’t deserve Geralt. Geralt is amazing. I do wish there were some more monster battles in this book. We did not get to see his full fighting greatness in this book. It is more about the coup and politics. I also miss him and Ciri traveling together. Together, they make such a great team and I have really enjoyed seeing Ciri learn from him. However, Ciri does need to discover herself. I did enjoy her storyline. She is going to be a badass just like Geralt—actually even more than Geralt.<br /><br />This book is a little slower than the rest of the series has been, but I have a feeling that it is mostly buildup for the next book, Baptism of Fire. I can’t wait to pick up the next book. I am hoping the Netflix Series really does the books justice! I rate this book 5 out of 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6798363149027921767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1217987547" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217987547" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217987547?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789863191230" href="/book/show/26541439">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217987547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18309352952515874881"><i>First thoughts after finished reading:</i>I don't want to judge too quickly, so I'll only rate this book after I finish reading its prequel (which is waiting for me in the library).<br/><br/>Still, I need to rant about a certain character: Ciri. I know, she is only a 14 years old girl in this book and teenagers aren't supposed to be mature and considerate and I know her parents and grandmother were killed when she was just a kid and she still has nightmares over the whole traumatic experiences and all, BUT sh</span>
  <span id="freeText18309352952515874881" style="display:none"><i>First thoughts after finished reading:</i>I don't want to judge too quickly, so I'll only rate this book after I finish reading its prequel (which is waiting for me in the library).<br /><br />Still, I need to rant about a certain character: Ciri. I know, she is only a 14 years old girl in this book and teenagers aren't supposed to be mature and considerate and I know her parents and grandmother were killed when she was just a kid and she still has nightmares over the whole traumatic experiences and all, BUT she really hasn't endeared herself to me in this book. I mean, by the end of the book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she gets transmitted magically (and accidentally) to a deadly desert and she is forced to struggle for survival AND THEN suddenly she decides her two guardians, Geralt and Yennefer <b>have always been lying to her</b> and she doesn't care about these two anymore!? She hasn't even once considered Geralt and Yennefer are out there doing what they can to save her, not once? And she doesn't care enough to check what have become of her guardians during the chaos? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That's just too freaking much.<br /><br /><b>Added thoughts after re-reading:</b><br /><br />It's a 3.8 stars fantasy read with great sense of humor. I like the story but I think there isn't enough action and stuff, the story is going somewhere but it isn't fast enough. However, I guess I just have to bring up more patience for the story, the characters and the author, which I'm pretty willing to do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18309352952515874881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hct8xx7UvRPfMVpiJSsbDBiukop+GKtH96TAqKo1I4UnYTyI5g3+d+f3OrxxNrO8+VHqRoyeWlWDstwL8UzT7Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mzfv8MSUCJSsdMIAaZUEvUIXERE2Rc6GmrdK3FIzTzM5na+/PE1L8JSyot49iKwNo+hp3cTDP5TuoVZ/CUq/Ww==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">About Andrzej Sapkowski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1241014902p3/38569.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">Andrzej Sapkowski
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11,112
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16706506846804024483">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. </span>
  <span id="freeText16706506846804024483" style="display:none">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. Sapkowski has created a cycle of tales based on the world of The Witcher, comprising three collections of short stories and five novels. This cycle and his many other works have made him one of the best-known fantasy authors in Poland in the 1990s.<br /><br />The main character of The Witcher (alternative translation: The Hexer) is Geralt, a mutant assassin who has been trained since childhood to hunt down and destroy monsters. Geralt exists in an ambiguous moral universe, yet manages to maintain his own coherent code of ethics. At the same time cynical and noble, Geralt has been compared to Raymond Chandler's signature character Philip Marlowe. The world in which these adventures take place is heavily influenced by Slavic mythology.<br /><br />Sapkowski has won five Zajdel Awards, including three for short stories "Mniejsze zło" (Lesser Evil) (1990), "Miecz przeznaczenia" (Sword of Destiny) (1992) and "W leju po bombie" (In a Bomb Crater) (1993), and two for the novels "Krew elfów" (Blood of Elves) (1994) and "Narrenturm" (2002). He also won the Spanish Ignotus Award, best anthology, for The Last Wish in 2003, and for "Muzykanci" (The Musicians), best foreign short story, same year.<br /><br />In 1997, Sapkowski won the prestigious Polityka's Passport award, which is awarded annually to artists who have strong prospects for international success.<br /><br />In 2001, a Television Series based on the Witcher cycle was released in Poland and internationally, entitled Wiedźmin (The Hexer). A film by the same title was compiled from excerpts of the television series but both have been critical and box office failures.<br /><br />Sapkowski's books have been translated into Czech, Russian, Lithuanian, German, Spanish, French, Ukrainian, and Portuguese. An English translation of The Last Wish short story collection was published by Gollancz in 2007.<br /><br />The Polish game publisher, CD Projekt, created a role-playing PC game based on this universe, called The Witcher, which was released in October 2007. There is also a mobile version of the game which has been created by Breakpoint Games and is being published by Hands-On Mobile in Western Europe,Latin America and Asia Pacific.<br /><br />The English translation of Sapkowski's novel Blood of Elves won the David Gemmell Legends Award in 2009.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16706506846804024483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1877759-czas-pogardy">Quotes from Czas pogardy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Why didn't you become a sorcerer, Geralt? Weren't you ever attracted by the Art? Be honest.'<br />'I will. I was.'<br />'Why, then, didn't you follow the voice of that attraction?'<br />'I decided it would be wiser to follow the voice of good sense.'<br />'Meaning?'<br />'Years of practice in the witcher's trade have taught me not to bite off more than I can chew. Do you know, Vilgefortz, I once knew a dwarf, who, as a child, dreamed of being an elf. What do you think; would he have become one had he followed the voice of attraction?&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/905884-why-didn-t-you-become-a-sorcerer-geralt-weren-t-you-ever">60 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Hmm…’ Ciri bit her lower lip, then leaned over and put her eye closer to the hole. ‘Madam Yennefer is standing by a willow… She’s plucking leaves and playing with her star. She isn’t saying anything and isn’t even looking at Geralt… And Geralt’s standing beside her. He’s looking down and he’s saying something. No, he isn’t. Oh, he’s pulling a face… What a strange expression…’ ‘Childishly simple,’ said Dandelion, finding an apple in the grass, wiping it on his trousers and examining it critically. ‘He’s asking her to forgive him for his various foolish words and deeds. He’s apologising to her for his impatience, for his lack of faith and hope, for his obstinacy, doggedness. For his sulking and posing; which are unworthy of a man. He’s apologising to her for things he didn’t understand and for things he hadn’t wanted to understand—’ ‘That’s the falsest lie!’ said Ciri, straightening up and tossing the fringe away from her forehead with a sudden movement. ‘You’re making it all up!’ ‘He’s apologising for things he’s only now understood,’ said Dandelion, staring at the sky, and he began to speak with the rhythm of a balladeer. ‘For what he’d like to understand, but is afraid he won’t have time for… And for what he will never understand. He’s apologising and asking for forgiveness… Hmm, hmm… Meaning, conscience, destiny? Everything’s so bloody banal…’ ‘That’s not true!’ Ciri stamped. ‘Geralt isn’t saying anything like that! He’s not even speaking. I saw for myself. He’s standing with her and saying nothing…’ ‘That’s the role of poetry, Ciri. To say what others cannot utter.’ ‘It’s a stupid role. And you’re making everything up!’ ‘That is also the role of poetry. Hey, I hear some raised voices coming from the pond. Have a quick look, and see what’s happening there.’ ‘Geralt,’ said Ciri, putting her eye once more to the hole in the wall, ‘is standing with his head bowed. And Yennefer’s yelling at him. She’s screaming and waving her arms. Oh dear… What can it mean?’ ‘It’s childishly simple.’ Dandelion stared at the clouds scudding across the sky. ‘Now she’s saying sorry to him.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1563112-hmm-ciri-bit-her-lower-lip-then-leaned-over-and">56 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
